# Investigation: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

**Repository:** grafana/grafana
**Task Type:** Regression Hunt (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After upgrading Grafana from v10.3 to v10.4, some dashboards with table panels fail to render correctly. The table panel's field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import. Users see tables with missing column formatting (column widths, text alignment, cell display modes).

The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON. Dashboards with explicit custom config render correctly.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Which migration function is responsible for the regression
2. The exact conditional logic that fails for dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`
3. Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected
4. Which dashboard schema version triggers the issue
5. The files and functions involved in the migration chain

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on the dashboard migration pipeline, particularly schema version handlers

     5→// V37 normalizes legend configuration to use `showLegend` property consistently.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses inconsistencies in how legend visibility was handled.
     8→// There were two ways to hide the legend:
     9→// 1. Using displayMode: "hidden"
    10→// 2. Using showLegend: false
    11→//
    12→// The migration normalizes both approaches to use showLegend consistently:
    13→// - If displayMode is "hidden" OR showLegend is false, set displayMode to "list" and showLegend to false
    14→// - For all other existing legend objects, ensure showLegend is true
    15→//
    16→// Note: This migration only processes legend configurations that already exist as objects.
    17→// Boolean legend values are not processed by this migration.
    18→//
    19→// Example transformations:
    20→//
    21→// Before migration (hidden displayMode):
    22→//
    23→//	options: {
    24→//	  legend: {
    25→//	    displayMode: "hidden",
    26→//	    placement: "bottom"
    27→//	  }
    28→//	}
    29→//
    30→// After migration:
    31→//
    32→//	options: {
    33→//	  legend: {
    34→//	    displayMode: "list",
    35→//	    showLegend: false,
    36→//	    placement: "bottom"
    37→//	  }
    38→//	}
    39→//
    40→// Before migration (showLegend false):
    41→//
    42→//	options: {
    43→//	  legend: {
    44→//	    displayMode: "table",
    45→//	    showLegend: false
    46→//	  }
    47→//	}
    48→//
    49→// After migration:
    50→//
    51→//	options: {
    52→//	  legend: {
    53→//	    displayMode: "list",
    54→//	    showLegend: false
    55→//	  }
    56→//	}

    59→//
    60→//	options: {

package schemaversion

import "context"

// V22 migrates table panel styles to set align property to 'auto'.
// This migration ensures that all table panel styles have their align property
// set to 'auto' for consistent alignment behavior.
//
// Example before migration:
//
//	"panels": [
//	  {
//	    "type": "table",
//	    "styles": [
//	      { "type": "number", "pattern": "Time", "align": "left" },
//	      { "type": "string", "pattern": "Value", "align": "right" }
//	    ]
//	  }
//	]
//
// Example after migration:
//
//	"panels": [
//	  {
//	    "type": "table",
//	    "styles": [
//	      { "type": "number", "pattern": "Time", "align": "auto" },
//	      { "type": "string", "pattern": "Value", "align": "auto" }
//	    ]
//	  }
//	]
func V22(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {
	dashboard["schemaVersion"] = 22

	panels, ok := dashboard["panels"].([]interface{})
	if !ok {
		return nil
	}

	for _, p := range panels {
		panel, ok := p.(map[string]interface{})
		if !ok {
			continue
		}

		// Only process table panels
		panelType, ok := panel["type"].(string)
		if !ok || panelType != "table" {
			continue
		}

		styles, ok := panel["styles"].([]interface{})
		if !ok {
			continue
		}

		// Update each style to set align to 'auto'
		for _, s := range styles {
			style, ok := s.(map[string]interface{})
			if !ok {
				continue
			}
			style["align"] = "auto"
		}
	}

	return nil
}

     8→func copyMap(src map[string]interface{}) map[string]interface{} {
     9→	dst := make(map[string]interface{})
    10→	for k, v := range src {
    11→		dst[k] = v
    12→	}
    13→	return dst
    14→}

    18→	if _, exists := obj[key]; exists {
    19→		t.Errorf("Property %s should have been removed but still exists", key)
    20→	}
    21→}

    26→		t.Errorf("Property %s should exist but is missing", key)
    27→	} else if !compareValues(actual, expected) {
    28→		t.Errorf("Property %s has wrong value. Expected: %v, Got: %v", key, expected, actual)
    29→	}
    30→}

    36→	}

   231→/**

   234→export function buildHeaderHeightMeasurers(
   235→  fields: Field[],
   236→  typographyCtx: TypographyCtx
   237→): MeasureCellHeightEntry[] | undefined {
   238→  const wrappedColIdxs = fields.reduce((acc: number[], field, idx) => {
   239→    if (field.config?.custom?.wrapHeaderText) {
   240→      acc.push(idx);
   241→    }
   242→    return acc;
   243→  }, []);
   244→
   245→  if (wrappedColIdxs.length === 0) {
   246→    return undefined;
   247→  }
   248→
   249→  // don't bother with estimating the line counts for the headers, because it's punishing
   250→  // when we get it wrong and there won't be that many compared to how many rows a table might contain.
   251→  return [{ measure: typographyCtx.measureHeight, fieldIdxs: wrappedColIdxs }];
   252→}

   769→export function migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayMode: TableCellDisplayMode): TableCellOptions {
   770→  switch (displayMode) {
   771→    // In the case of the gauge we move to a different option
   772→    case TableCellDisplayMode.BasicGauge:
   773→    case TableCellDisplayMode.GradientGauge:
   774→    case TableCellDisplayMode.LcdGauge:
   775→      return {
   776→        type: TableCellDisplayMode.Gauge,
   777→        mode: TABLE_CELL_GAUGE_DISPLAY_MODES_TO_DISPLAY_MODES[displayMode],
   778→      };
   779→    // Also true in the case of the color background
   780→    case TableCellDisplayMode.ColorBackground:
   781→    case TableCellDisplayMode.ColorBackgroundSolid:
   782→      return {
   783→        type: TableCellDisplayMode.ColorBackground,
   784→        mode: TABLE_CELL_COLOR_BACKGROUND_DISPLAY_MODES_TO_DISPLAY_MODES[displayMode],
   785→      };
   786→    // catching a nonsense case: `displayMode`: 'custom' should pre-date the CustomCell.
   787→    // if it doesn't, we need to just nope out and return an auto cell.
   788→    case TableCellDisplayMode.Custom:
   789→      return {
   790→        type: TableCellDisplayMode.Auto,
   791→      };
   792→    default:
   793→      return {
   794→        type: displayMode,
   795→      };
   796→  }
   797→}
   798→

   800→ * @internal
   801→ * Returns true if the DataFrame contains nested frames

   803→export const getIsNestedTable = (fields: Field[]): boolean =>
   804→  fields.some(({ type }) => type === FieldType.nestedFrames);

## Summary of Findings: Table Panel Migration Code Analysis

Based on my thorough search of the grafana/grafana codebase, I've identified the table panel migration code and the potential issue with field override configuration handling. Here are my findings:

### 1. **Table Panel Migration Code Location**

**Primary Files:**
- `/workspace/public/app/plugins/panel/table/migrations.ts` - Frontend table panel migrations
- `/workspace/public/app/plugins/panel/table/migrations.test.ts` - Comprehensive tests
- `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go` - Backend dashboard migration logic with fieldConfig handling
- `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go` - Main migration entry point

### 2. **Key Table Migration Functions**

**Frontend (`migrations.ts`):**
- `tableMigrationHandler()` - Main migration handler for table panels
- `tablePanelChangedHandler()` - Handles migration when changing from angular table (`table-old`) to react table
- `migrateTableStyleToOverride()` - Converts old table styles to fieldConfig overrides
- `migrateDefaults()` - Converts old table defaults to fieldConfig.defaults.custom
- `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel()` - Migrates wrapText from cellOptions to field level
- `migrateHiddenFields()` - Migrates hidden field configuration
- `migrateFooterV2()` - Migrates footer configuration from options to fieldConfig

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor

216-assistanttext-
The investigation is complete. Here's a summary of the findings:

**Root cause:** In `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:120-123`, the `processPanelsV38()` function chains three type assertions — for `fieldConfig`, `defaults`, and `custom` — and uses `continue` to bail out of the entire loop iteration if any fails. The `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call at line 135 is unreachable when `defaults["custom"]` is absent, even though field overrides live in `fieldConfig["overrides"]`, a completely independent path.

**Why the frontend works:** The TypeScript equivalent in `DashboardMigrator.ts:644-669` uses optional chaining (`?.`) to safely check `defaults.custom.displayMode` without short-circuiting, and processes overrides in a separate `if` block that only requires `fieldConfig` to exist.

**Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected:** When `defaults.custom` is present (even as an empty `{}`), the type assertion at line 120 succeeds, the `continue` is not hit, and `migrateOverrides()` executes normally on line 135.

**Schema version:** Dashboards with `schemaVersion` <= 37 trigger V38 migration. The migration is registered at `migrations.go:74`.

The full report with file paths, line numbers, and a recommended fix strategy has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

404\u2192\t\t\t\t\tletterIndex++\n   405\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   406\u2192\t\t\t}\n   407\u2192\t\t}\n   408\u2192\t}\n   409\u2192}\n   410\u2192\n   411\u2192// getPanels extracts all panels from the isEqual(a, b interface{}) bool {\n   666\u2192\tif a == nil && b == nil {\n   667\u2192\t\treturn true\n   668\u2192\t}\n   669\u2192\tif a == nil || b == nil {\n   670\u2192\t\treturn false\n   671\u2192\t}\n   672\u2192\n   673\u2192\t// For simple types, use direct comparison\n   674\u2192\tswitch aVal := a.(type) {\n   675\u2192\tcase bool:\n   676\u2192\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(bool); ok {\n   677\u2192\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n   678\u2192\t\t}\n   679\u2192\tcase string:\n   680\u2192\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(string); ok {\n   681\u2192\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n   682\u2192\t\t}\n   683\u2192\tcase float64:\n   684\u2192\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(float64); ok {\n   685\u2192\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n   686\u2192\t\t}\n   687\u2192\tcase []interface{}:\n   688\u2192\t\tif bVal, ok := b.([]interface{}); ok {\n   689\u2192\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n   690\u2192\t\t\t\treturn false\n   691\u2192\t\t\t}\n   692\u2192\t\t\tfor i, v := range aVal {\n   693\u2192\t\t\t\tif !isEqual(v, bVal[i]) {\n   694\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn false\n   695\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   696\u2192\t\t\t}\n   697\u2192\t\t\treturn true\n   698\u2192\t\t}\n   699\u2192\tcase map[string]interface{}:\n   700\u2192\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   701\u2192\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n   702\u2192\t\t\t\treturn false\n   703\u2192\t\t\t}\n   704\u2192\t\t\tfor k, v := range aVal {\n   705\u2192\t\t\t\tif !isEqual(v, bVal[k]) {\n   706\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn false\n   707\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   708\u2192\t\t\t}\n   709\u2192\t\t\treturn true\n   710\u2192\t\t}\n   711\u2192\t}\n   712\u2192\n   713\u2192\treturn false\n   714\u2192}\n   715\u2192\n   716\u2192// cleanupDashboardForSave applies the same cleanup logic as the frontend\n   717\u2192func 39\u2192```\n    40\u2192v0alpha1 (Legacy JSON) \u2192 v1beta1 (Migrated JSON) \u2192 v2alpha1/v2beta1 (Structured)\n    41\u2192```\n    42\u2192\n    43\u2192#### v0 to v1 Conversion:\n    44\u2192- 54\u2192- Handles modern dashboard features and Kubernetes-native storage\n    55\u2192\n    56\u2192## Conversion Matrix\n    57\u2192\n    58\u2192The system supports conversions between all dashboard API versions:\n    59\u2192\n    60\u2192| From \u2193 / To \u2192 | v0alpha1 | v1beta1 | v2alpha1 | v2beta1 |\n    61\u2192|---------------|----------|---------|----------|---------|\n  72\u2192\n    73\u2192- `dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1` - Legacy JSON dashboard format\n    74\u2192- `dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1` - Migrated JSON dashboard format  \n    75\u2192-    79\u2192\n    80\u2192Schema versions (v13-v42) apply only to v0alpha1 and v1beta1 dashboards:\n    81\u2192\n    82\u2192- **Minimum supported version**: v13\n    83\u2192- **Latest version**: v42  \n    84\u2192- **Migration path**: Sequential (v13\u2192v14\u2192v15...\u2192v42)\n    85\u2192\n    86\u2192For detailed information about creating schema version migrations, see the [SchemaVersion provides comprehensive observability through:\n   144\u2192- **Prometheus metrics** for tracking conversion success/failure rates and performance\n   145\u2192- **Structured logging** for debugging and monitoring conversion operations\n   146\u2192- **Automatic instrumentation** via wrapper functions that eliminate code duplication\n   147\u2192- **Error classification** to distinguish between different types of migration failures\n   148\u2192\n   149\u2192#### 1. Dashboard conversion success metric\n   150\u2192\n   151\u2192**Metric Name:** `grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total`\n   152\u2192\n   153\u2192**Type:** Counter\n   154\u2192\n   155\u2192**Description:** Total number of successful dashboard conversions\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192**Labels:**\n   158\u2192- `source_version_api` - Source API version (e.g., \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\")\n   159\u2192- `target_version_api` - Target API version (e.g., \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\")\n   160\u2192- `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (e.g., \"16\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\n   161\u2192- `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (e.g., \"41\") - only for v0/v1 dashboards\n   162\u2192\n   163\u2192**Example:**\n   164\u2192```prometheus\n   165\u2192grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_success_total{\n   166\u2192  source_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n   167\u2192  target_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n   168\u2192  source_schema_version=\"16\",\n   169\u2192  target_schema_version=\"41\"\n   170\u2192} 1250\n   171\u2192```\n   172\u2192\n   173\u2192#### 2. 179\u2192**Description:** Total number of failed dashboard conversions\n   180\u2192\n   181\u2192**Labels:**\n   182\u2192- `source_version_api` - Source API version\n   183\u2192- `target_version_api` - Target API version  \n   184\u2192- `source_schema_version` - Source schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\n   185\u2192- `target_schema_version` - Target schema version (only for v0/v1 dashboards)\n   186\u2192- `error_type` - Classification of the error (see Error Types section)\n   187\u2192\n   188\u2192**Example:**\n   189\u2192```prometheus\n   190\u2192grafana_dashboard_migration_conversion_failure_total{\n   191\u2192  source_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n   192\u2192  target_version_api=\"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n   193\u2192  source_schema_version=\"14\",\n   194\u2192  target_schema_version=\"41\",\n   195\u2192  error_type=\"schema_version_migration_error\"\n   196\u2192} 42\n   197\u2192```\n   198\u2192\n   199\u2192### Error Types\n   200\u2192\n   201\u2192The `error_type` label classifies failures into three categories:\n   202\u2192\n   203\u2192#### 1. `conversion_error`\n   204\u2192- General conversion failures not related to schema migration\n   205\u2192- API-level conversion issues\n   206\u2192- Programming errors in conversion functions\n   207\u2192\n   208\u2192#### 2. `schema_version_migration_error`\n   209\u2192- Failures during individual schema version migrations (v14\u2192v15, v15\u2192v16, etc.)\n   210\u2192- Schema-specific transformation errors\n   211\u2192- Data format incompatibilities\n   212\u2192\n   213\u2192#### 3. `schema_minimum_version_error`\n   214\u2192- Dashboards with schema versions below the minimum supported version (< v13)\n   215\u2192- These are logged as warnings rather than errors\n   216\u2192- Indicates dashboards that cannot be migrated automatically\n   217\u2192\n   218\u2192### Logging\n   219\u2192\n   220\u2192#### Log structure\n   221\u2192\n   222\u2192All migration logs use structured logging with consistent field names:\n   223\u2192\n   224\u2192**Base Fields (always present):**\n   225\u2192- `sourceVersionAPI` - Source API version\n   226\u2192- `targetVersionAPI` - Target API version\n   227\u2192- `dashboardUID` - Unique identifier of the dashboard being converted\n   228\u2192\n   229\u2192**Schema Version Fields (v0/v1 dashboards only):**\n   230\u2192- `sourceSchemaVersion` - Source schema version number\n   231\u2192- `targetSchemaVersion` - Target schema version number\n   232\u2192- `erroredSchemaVersionFunc` - Name of the schema migration function that failed (on error)\n   233\u2192\n   234\u2192**Error Fields (failures only):**\n   235\u2192- `errorType` - Same classification as metrics error_type label\n   236\u2192- `erroredConversionFunc` - Name of the conversion function that failed\n   237\u2192- `error` - The actual error message\n   238\u2192\n   239\u2192#### Log levels\n   240\u2192\n   241\u2192##### Success (DEBUG level)\n   242\u2192```json\n   243\u2192{\n   244\u2192  \"level\": \"debug\",\n   245\u2192  \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion succeeded\",\n   246\u2192  \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n   247\u2192  \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n   248\u2192  \"dashboardUID\": \"abc123\",\n   249\u2192  \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 16,\n   250\u2192  \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41\n   251\u2192}\n   252\u2192```\n   253\u2192\n   254\u2192##### Conversion/Migration Error (ERROR level)\n   255\u2192```json\n   256\u2192{\n   257\u2192  \"level\": \"error\", \n   258\u2192  \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion failed\",\n   259\u2192  \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n   260\u2192  \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n   261\u2192  \"erroredConversionFunc\": \"Convert_V0_to_V1\",\n   262\u2192  \"dashboardUID\": \"abc123\",\n   263\u2192  \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 16,\n   264\u2192  \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41,\n   265\u2192  \"erroredSchemaVersionFunc\": \"V24\",\n   266\u2192  \"errorType\": \"schema_version_migration_error\",\n   267\u2192  \"error\": \"migration failed: table panel plugin not found\"\n   268\u2192}\n   269\u2192```\n   270\u2192\n   271\u2192##### Minimum Version Error (WARN level)\n   272\u2192```json\n   273\u2192{\n   274\u2192  \"level\": \"warn\",\n   275\u2192  \"msg\": \"Dashboard conversion failed\", \n   276\u2192  \"sourceVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v0alpha1\",\n   277\u2192  \"targetVersionAPI\": \"dashboard.grafana.app/v1beta1\",\n   278\u2192  \"erroredConversionFunc\": \"Convert_V0_to_V1\",\n   279\u2192  \"dashboardUID\": \"def456\",\n   280\u2192  \"sourceSchemaVersion\": 10,\n   281\u2192  \"targetSchemaVersion\": 41,\n   282\u2192  \"erroredSchemaVersionFunc\": \"\",\n   283\u2192  \"errorType\": \"schema_minimum_version_error\",\n   284\u2192  \"error\": \"dashboard schema version 10 cannot be migrated\"\n   285\u2192}\n   286\u2192```\n   287\u2192\n   288\u2192### Implementation Details\n   289\u2192\n   290\u2192#### Automatic instrumentation\n   291\u2192\n   292\u2192All dashboard conversions are automatically instrumented via the `withConversionMetrics` wrapper function:\n   293\u2192\n   294\u2192```go\n   295\u2192// All conversion functions are wrapped automatically\n   296\u2192s.AddConversionFunc((*dashv0.Dashboard)(nil), (*dashv1.Dashboard)(nil),\n   297\u2192    withConversionMetrics(dashv0.APIVERSION, dashv1.APIVERSION, func(a, b interface{}, scope conversion.Scope) error {\n   298\u2192        return Convert_V0_to_V1(a.(*dashv0.Dashboard), b.(*dashv1.Dashboard), scope)\n   299\u2192    }))\n   300\u2192```\n   301\u2192\n   302\u2192#### Error handling\n   303\u2192\n   304\u2192Custom error types provide structured error information:\n   305\u2192\n   306\u2192```go\n   307\u2192// Schema migration errors\n   308\u2192type MigrationError struct {\n   309\u2192    msg            string\n   310\u2192    targetVersion  int\n   311\u2192    currentVersion int\n   312\u2192    functionName   string\n   313\u2192}\n   314\u2192\n   315\u2192// API conversion errors  \n   316\u2192type ConversionError struct {\n   317\u2192    msg               string\n   318\u2192    functionName      string\n   319\u2192    currentAPIVersion string\n   320\u2192    targetAPIVersion  string\n   321\u2192}\n   322\u2192```\n   323\u2192\n   324\u2192### Registration\n   325\u2192\n   326\u2192#### Metrics registration\n   327\u2192\n   328\u2192Metrics must be registered with Prometheus Prometheus\n   334\u2192migration.RegisterMetrics(prometheusRegistry)\n   335\u2192```\n   336\u2192\n   337\u2192#### Available metrics\n   338\u2192\n   339\u2192The following metrics are available Type Assertions\n   369\u2192```go\n   370\u2192// \u274c Wrong - can panic\n   371\u2192value := panel[\"property\"].(string)\n   372\u2192\n   373\u2192// \u2705 Correct - safe type assertion\n   374\u2192if value, ok := panel[\"property\"].(string); ok {\n   375\u2192\t// Use value\n   376\u2192}\n   377\u2192```\n   378\u2192\n   379\u2192### 2. Null Handling\n   380\u2192```go\n   381\u2192// \u274c Wrong - removes intentional nulls\n   382\u2192if value == nil {\n   383\u2192\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n   384\u2192}\n   385\u2192\n   386\u2192// \u2705 Correct - preserve intentional nulls\n   387\u2192if value == nil && !isIntentionallyNull(panel, \"property\") {\n   388\u2192\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n   389\u2192}\n   390\u2192```\n   391\u2192\n   392\u2192### 3. For new migrations beyond v42:\n   408\u2192\n   409\u21921. **Backend**: Continue adding schema versions in Go\n   410\u21922. **Frontend**: Use panel-specific migration handlers instead of schema versions\n   411\u21923. **Justification Required**: Each new migration must be properly justified\n   412\u21924. **v2 Transition**: Consider the impact on the transition to schema v2\n   413\u2192\n   414\u2192### When to Add Schema Migrations vs Panel Migrations\n   415\u2192\n   416\u2192**Add Schema Migration** when:\n   417\u2192- Changes affect dashboard-level properties\n   418\u2192- Cross-panel transformations are needed\n   419\u2192- Backward compatibility requires schema version increment\n   420\u2192- **With proper justification** about why it can't be handled as panel     "content": "package schemaversion\n\nimport \"context\"\n\n// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.\n//\n// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where\n// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering\n// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it\n// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.\n//\n// The migration works by:\n// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)\n// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties\n// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode\n// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path\n// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features\n//\n// This restructuring provides several key benefits:\n// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)\n// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations\n// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode\n// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality\n//\n// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,\n// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.\n//\n// Example transformations:\n//\n// Before migration (field defaults):\n//\n//\tfieldConfig: {\n//\t  defaults: {\n//\t    custom: {\n//\t      displayMode: \"gradient-gauge\"\n//\t    }\n//\t  }\n//\t}\n//\n// After migration (field defaults):\n//\n//\tfieldConfig: {\n//\t  defaults: {\n//\t    custom: {\n//\t      cellOptions: {\n//\t [{\n//\t  matcher: { id: \"byName\", options: \"CPU\" },\n//\t  properties: [{\n//\t    id: \"custom.cellOptions\",\n//\t    value: {\n//\t      type: \"color-background\",\n//\t      mode: {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tcustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions\n\t\tif displayMode,   "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nThe backend V38 schema migration in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go` gates the entire panel processing \u2014 including field override migration \u2014 behind a `defaults[\"custom\"]` type assertion that bails out with `continue` when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is absent. The frontend equivalent (`DashboardMigrator.ts`) processes overrides independently of whether `defaults.custom` exists, so dashboards that lack an explicit `defaults.custom` object have their overrides correctly migrated on the frontend but silently skipped on the backend.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n**Function:** `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)\n\nThe function chains three sequential type assertions before reaching the override migration call:\n\n```go\n// Line 110-113: gate 1 \u2014 fieldConfig must exist\nfieldConfig, ok := p[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n\n// Line 115-118: gate 2 \u2014 defaults must exist\ndefaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n\n// Line 120-123: gate 3 \u2014 custom must exist  *** THIS IS THE BUG ***\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue   // <-- skips the ENTIRE rest of the loop body, including migrateOverrides()\n}\n\n// Line 125-132: migrate displayMode in defaults.custom (only relevant if custom exists)\nif displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists { ... }\n\n// Line 134-135: migrate overrides (SHOULD run even without defaults.custom)\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n```\n\nThe `continue` on line 122 aborts the entire panel processing iteration. The `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135 is unreachable when `defaults[\"custom\"]` is nil or absent, even though overrides live in `fieldConfig[\"overrides\"]` \u2014 a completely independent path from `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`.\n\n**Contrast with the frontend** (`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`, lines 644-669):\n\n```typescript\nif (panel.type === 'table' && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined) {\n    // defaults.custom migration is guarded independently\n    const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;\n    if (displayMode !== undefined) {\n        // ... migrate defaults.custom.displayMode ...\n    }\n\n    // Override migration runs UNCONDITIONALLY (only gated on fieldConfig existing)\n    if (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n        for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) { ... }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe frontend uses optional chaining (`?.`) to safely access `defaults.custom.displayMode` without short-circuiting the rest of the function. The override migration block is a separate `if` statement that runs regardless of whether `defaults.custom` exists.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Backend V38 \u2014 bail-out chain (v38.go:120-123)\n\n`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go:120-123`:\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n```\n\nThis `continue` skips `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` at line 135.\n\n### 2. Frontend V38 \u2014 independent override processing (DashboardMigrator.ts:658-669)\n\n`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts:658-669`:\n```typescript\n// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\nif (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n    for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) {\n        for (let j = 0; j < (override.properties?.length || 0); j++) {\n            let overrideDisplayMode = override.properties[j].value;\n            if (override.properties[j].id === 'custom.displayMode') {\n                override.properties[j].id = 'custom.cellOptions';\n                override.properties[j].value = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(overrideDisplayMode);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis block is NOT nested inside any `defaults.custom` check.\n\n### 3. Backend test suite only tests panels WITH defaults.custom (v38_test.go)\n\n`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`: Every test panel includes an explicit `\"custom\": map[string]interface{}{...}` in defaults. There is no test case for a table panel that has `fieldConfig.overrides` with `custom.displayMode` properties but lacks `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`. This gap allowed the regression to pass tests.\n\n### 4. Post-migration cleanup compounds the issue (frontend_defaults.go:557-662)\n\n`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go:557-662`: The `filterDefaultValues` function and `cleanupPanelForSaveWithContext` (line 440) interact with a tracking marker `_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom`. When a panel lacks `defaults.custom`:\n\n- `trackPanelOriginalFieldConfigCustom` (line 1151-1158) does NOT set the marker\n- During cleanup, `filterDefaultValues` compares the panel's `fieldConfig` against the default `{\"defaults\": {}, \"overrides\": []}` (line 576-579)\n- If overrides were not migrated (still contain `custom.displayMode` instead of `custom.cellOptions`), the overrides remain as-is\n- However, the un-migrated `custom.displayMode` override property IDs are stale and no longer recognized by the table panel renderer in v10.4, causing the overrides to be silently ignored at render time\n\n### 5. Schema version trigger\n\n`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/migrations.go:74`: The V38 migration is registered for schema version 38. Dashboards with `schemaVersion` <= 37 trigger this migration during import. The handoff version is 36 (`pkg/kinds/dashboard/addenda.go`), meaning dashboards at version 36 or 37 go through the backend V38 migration path.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`** \u2014 `processPanelsV38()` function: the bail-out `continue` on line 122 is the root cause\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`** \u2014 missing test coverage for panels without `defaults.custom` but with overrides\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go`** \u2014 orchestrates the migration pipeline; calls V38 at line 120-126\n- **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go`** \u2014 `trackOriginalFieldConfigCustom()` (line 1140) and `filterDefaultValues()` (line 557) interact with the marker system; while not the direct cause, the cleanup logic's reconstruction at line 637-643 creates an empty overrides array `[]interface{}{}` which would also discard overrides if fieldConfig were removed and reconstructed\n- **`public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`** \u2014 the frontend counterpart (lines 644-674) handles this correctly; the discrepancy is backend-only\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix should restructure `processPanelsV38()` in `v38.go` to decouple the `defaults.custom` check from the override migration. The `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call must execute for any table panel that has a `fieldConfig`, regardless of whether `defaults.custom` exists.\n\nSpecifically:\n\n1. **Move `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` outside the `defaults[\"custom\"]` guard.** The override migration should be gated only on `fieldConfig` existing (matching the frontend behavior), not on `defaults.custom` existing.\n\n2. **Add a test case** to `v38_test.go` for a table panel with:\n   - `fieldConfig.defaults` set to `{}` (no `custom` key)\n   - `fieldConfig.overrides` containing `custom.displayMode` properties\n   - Expected output: overrides migrated to `custom.cellOptions` format, defaults unchanged\n\n3. The restructured logic should look like:\n   ```go\n   // Migrate defaults.custom.displayMode if custom exists\n   if custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n       if displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n           if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n               custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n           }\n           delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n       }\n   }\n   // Always migrate overrides (independent of defaults.custom)\n   migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)\n   ```\n",

# Investigation Report

## Summary

The backend V38 schema migration in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go` gates the entire panel processing — including field override migration — behind a `defaults["custom"]` type assertion that bails out with `continue` when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is absent. The frontend equivalent (`DashboardMigrator.ts`) processes overrides independently of whether `defaults.custom` exists, so dashboards that lack an explicit `defaults.custom` object have their overrides correctly migrated on the frontend but silently skipped on the backend.

## Root Cause

**File:** `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`
**Function:** `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)

The function chains three sequential type assertions before reaching the override migration call:

```go
// Line 110-113: gate 1 — fieldConfig must exist
fieldConfig, ok := p["fieldConfig"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue
}

// Line 115-118: gate 2 — defaults must exist
defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue
}

// Line 120-123: gate 3 — custom must exist  *** THIS IS THE BUG ***
custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue   // <-- skips the ENTIRE rest of the loop body, including migrateOverrides()
}

// Line 125-132: migrate displayMode in defaults.custom (only relevant if custom exists)
if displayMode, exists := custom["displayMode"]; exists { ... }

// Line 134-135: migrate overrides (SHOULD run even without defaults.custom)
migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)
```

The `continue` on line 122 aborts the entire panel processing iteration. The `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` call on line 135 is unreachable when `defaults["custom"]` is nil or absent, even though overrides l
... (truncated)
